    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1193858471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1193858471" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1193858471?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=orphalins">orphalins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=books-i-missed-during-childhood">books-i-missed-during-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=class-gender-race">class-gender-race</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=schools-of-magic">schools-of-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193858471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14851280351057837871"><i>Daja’s Book</i> is the third in Tamora Pierce’s children’s fantasy book series, Circle of Magic. I was previously classifying this as young adult, but this book has firmly set my mind on the subject. At the end of these books, I keep wanting more from them. More development. More sophistication. More actual content (they’re very short). More time spent (they take place over very short periods of time). And I finally decided, basically just about five minutes ago, that the expectations I was placing </span>
  <span id="freeText14851280351057837871" style="display:none"><i>Daja’s Book</i> is the third in Tamora Pierce’s children’s fantasy book series, Circle of Magic. I was previously classifying this as young adult, but this book has firmly set my mind on the subject. At the end of these books, I keep wanting more from them. More development. More sophistication. More actual content (they’re very short). More time spent (they take place over very short periods of time). And I finally decided, basically just about five minutes ago, that the expectations I was placing on this series are not ones it’s designed to meet. Tammy’s other books (in Tortall with Alanna and company) are what I’m used to from her, and have much more complexity, length, etc. These are skewed younger, so I have to remind myself to evaluate them on that level.<br /> <br />And on that level, they are really freaking fantastic.<br /> <br />This time around it’s Daja’s turn to have a feature story, and it’s a pretty great one. The kids’ magics are even more tied up with each other than in the last book, to the point where it’s endangering them. So they have to sort that out. Also, they’re out touring the countryside with their teachers, who are helping maintain local communities beset with drought and fires. In the midst of this, Daja accidentally creates a living plant made out of iron, and attracts the attention of her former people, the Traders, who had banished her and named her persona non grata (essentially). So she’s also got to deal with her heritage and the prejudicial nature of her home culture. As always, Tammy books do a deft job exploring power dynamics between genders, cultures, classes, all that stuff. But she does it subtly and with cool magic and characters you can love.<br /> <br />If I ever have kids, this is a series I will definitely be giving them, although I do hope that in future installments of the Emelan world that the kids are a bit more grown up, and the books reflect that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14851280351057837871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1313580011578205313">I really loved this book. The only reason it's four stars instead of five stars is because I didn't connect at all with some of the magic used here- there are times of the kids being magically away from their bodies, and that completely takes me out of the experience of the book.<br/><br/>But that is literally my only complaint. Tamora Pierce does yet another fantastic job of writing young heroines realistically and powerfully. Daja Kisubo shines extremely brightly in this book. It continues the story of </span>
  <span id="freeText1313580011578205313" style="display:none">I really loved this book. The only reason it's four stars instead of five stars is because I didn't connect at all with some of the magic used here- there are times of the kids being magically away from their bodies, and that completely takes me out of the experience of the book.<br /><br />But that is literally my only complaint. Tamora Pierce does yet another fantastic job of writing young heroines realistically and powerfully. Daja Kisubo shines extremely brightly in this book. It continues the story of all of the kids, of course, and strengthens the CIRCLE OF FRIENDSHIP even further, but what stands out for me as different from Tris's Book is that Daja grows here, but only becomes truly more of who she is. Her goodness emanates out of her. Tris had to learn some other lessons for her growth, and was much more flawed than Daja is naturally (and I love Tris for it!). <br /><br />This book also gives us a big glance into a particular part of Trader culture, and the story within that is my favorite of the Emelan stories so far- which is all I'll say as I don't want to give anything away! I will note that I hope Polyam returns in future books. :-) </span>
  <a data-text-id="1313580011578205313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2240704980" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240704980" />
    <a title="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book"><img alt="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498969347p2/39496028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2240704980?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)" href="/user/show/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book">Abi (The Knights Who Say Book)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=best-fantasy">best-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=read-multiple-times">read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39496028-abi-the-knights-who-say-book?shelf=main-character-of-color">main-character-of-color</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2240704980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14392775291688327904"><b>2020 Review:</b> Still love how much we learn about the traders in this book! I like that there are really solid differences between trader culture and dominant Emelan culture, it's not just skin-deep. So many books will have a people who lives on the road but completely fail to develop them as their own culture, but this book doesn't do that.<br/><br/>I wish we got to see Daja make more living metal plants in the future, because that's also a really cool part of this book.<br/><br/><b>2018 Review:</b> Ugh, these audiobooks a</span>
  <span id="freeText14392775291688327904" style="display:none"><b>2020 Review:</b> Still love how much we learn about the traders in this book! I like that there are really solid differences between trader culture and dominant Emelan culture, it's not just skin-deep. So many books will have a people who lives on the road but completely fail to develop them as their own culture, but this book doesn't do that.<br /><br />I wish we got to see Daja make more living metal plants in the future, because that's also a really cool part of this book.<br /><br /><b>2018 Review:</b> Ugh, these audiobooks are great but they take so much longer to finish than a physical book, so by the time I'm writing the review the beginning is kinda faded.<br /><br />Anyway, finally reading this series continues to be a great idea. I love how this book really delves into Daja's feelings about being isolated from her people while keeping the relationship among the four kids as a focus too. You can tell this book has really grabbed my emotional investment because I was just as upset about what might happen to their intertwined magic as they were.<br /><br />Other great things about this book were that weird magical metal plant Daja made, Polyam's entire character, and seeing the kids outside of Winding Circle. I think I was sort of put off by them suddenly being outside the temple community in the beginning, but eventually I realized it's a great way to challenge them, and cool to see how their little <i>circle of magic</i> clashes with the rest of the world. I also like how Yarrun looked like a bit of a cliche evil sorcerer in the beginning but he kind of turned into this nuanced tragic figure.<br /><br />Also, the ending is great and made me think that this might be my favorite of the series. I don't know yet, because I have to read Briar's Book to finish up and I do think all three of the ones I've read have both their strengths and weaknesses. But Daja's Book is definitely a great installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14392775291688327904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_310516769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310516769" />
    <a title="Fuchsia Rascal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/394650-fuchsia-rascal"><img alt="Fuchsia Rascal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359831216p2/394650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310516769?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuchsia Rascal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuchsia Rascal" href="/user/show/394650-fuchsia-rascal">Fuchsia Rascal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780590553582" href="/book/show/793813.Daja_s_Book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=rereadin2012">rereadin2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=women-rock">women-rock</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=women-writer">women-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/394650-fuchsia-rascal?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310516769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15704686745545096880">While Tris's Book was a little weak and closely followed the pattern of Sandry's Book, Daja's Book mixes things up and it definitely benefits from this. The group is journeying with Sandry's uncle, trying to help areas that have been hit hard by drought and failing crops. The change of scenery is extremely refreshing for this series-- we get a lot of new characters, and our main cast is bumped out of their routines from Winding Circle. The focus, obviously, is on Daja, and it delves deep into he</span>
  <span id="freeText15704686745545096880" style="display:none">While Tris's Book was a little weak and closely followed the pattern of Sandry's Book, Daja's Book mixes things up and it definitely benefits from this. The group is journeying with Sandry's uncle, trying to help areas that have been hit hard by drought and failing crops. The change of scenery is extremely refreshing for this series-- we get a lot of new characters, and our main cast is bumped out of their routines from Winding Circle. The focus, obviously, is on Daja, and it delves deep into her Trader identity, but Briar gets a lot of attention as well [setting up nicely for the next book]. I won't lie, I find Daja's magic extremely fascinating, but even that pales in comparison to what's really going on with the four's powers. Woven together by Sandry a few months ago, we saw some bleed-through of their magics in the previous book but here, they have serious consequences. Daja loses control of her magic and creates living metal, and Briar accidentally fries some plants when lightning jumps from his fingers. It's natural that the weaving of their powers resulted in this, but these new powers can be both a benefit and a disaster. I loved to see them deal with these results and it really showed how far these children have come in just a few months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15704686745545096880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer743564979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17708922429482877984">Daja, Tris, Briar, and Sandry are traveling Emelan with the Duke to see what they can do about the drought and subsequent famine that is plaguing the area. During this tour, Daja runs into a group of traders - people of the culture that shunned her after her entire family died at sea. But when disaster strikes, will the Traders allow Daja to help or will their pride get in the way?<br/><br/>I am crazy about this entire series, it is one of my constant rereads. Daja is an amazingly courageous individual an</span>
  <span id="freeText17708922429482877984" style="display:none">Daja, Tris, Briar, and Sandry are traveling Emelan with the Duke to see what they can do about the drought and subsequent famine that is plaguing the area. During this tour, Daja runs into a group of traders - people of the culture that shunned her after her entire family died at sea. But when disaster strikes, will the Traders allow Daja to help or will their pride get in the way?<br /><br />I am crazy about this entire series, it is one of my constant rereads. Daja is an amazingly courageous individual and I have nothing but the utmost respect for her. Her family dies and she gets exiled from the only life she's ever known but she is still so forgiving of her people. I honestly don't know that I could say that. Daja is more gracious than she has any right to be. Highly recommended!</span>

<div id="review_1198775792" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198775792" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198775792?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613284608" href="/book/show/879218.Daja_s_Book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198775792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5403618033295764838">Third in the Circle of Magic fantasy series for young middle-grade readers and revolving around four young friends tied together by magic.<br/><br/><em>Daja's Book</em> was nominated for the Mythopoeic Fantasy Award for Children's Literature in 2000.<br/><br/>Visit <a href='http://kddidit.com/reading-books/series-info/chronological-lists-of-complex-intersected-series/#emelan' rel='nofollow noopener'>KD Did It Takes on Books</a> for a chronological listing of the books in the Circle of Magic series.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>After two books of adventure, the kids are amazing together. It's teamwork and friendship as they come to a greater understanding of how the magic bond they sha</span>
  <span id="freeText5403618033295764838" style="display:none">Third in the Circle of Magic fantasy series for young middle-grade readers and revolving around four young friends tied together by magic.<br /><br /><em>Daja's Book</em> was nominated for the Mythopoeic Fantasy Award for Children's Literature in 2000.<br /><br />Visit <a href="http://kddidit.com/reading-books/series-info/chronological-lists-of-complex-intersected-series/#emelan" rel="nofollow noopener">KD Did It Takes on Books</a> for a chronological listing of the books in the Circle of Magic series.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />After two books of adventure, the kids are amazing together. It's teamwork and friendship as they come to a greater understanding of how the magic bond they share works. Talking about support, I absolutely adored (and laughed) when Sandry, Briar, and Tris stood up for Daja and forced Polyam to treat Daja with politeness and <em>all</em> the trimmings.<br /><br />Daja discovers a new ability by accident, growing metal into a plant with leaves that grow. It also brings her courage, the confidence to insist on bargaining directly with the Traders.<br /><br />Ooh, that rivalry between Niko and Firetamer is intense, and one of the reasons for Firetamer's insecurity. There's a good lesson in here for your own children, one of accepting one's limitations. Of becoming comfortable with it, but not complacent. There's also an environmental lesson in here, one we've only come to understand these past few decades about the importance of fire in a forest. A secondary lesson in this is that one never stops learning. <em>God knows I'm always learning something new!</em><br /><br />Sandry has a nice bit of wisdom for Daja, that since she is no longer a Trader, she is her own person. That she can make her own status, to stand up for herself. Daja raises her own questions about fame and envy.<br /><br />I hate people like those in Gold Ridge, more interested in status and showing off.<br /><br />That was unfair of Niko, scolding the kids for something they did when he never said anything before.<br /><br />Little bits of background are dropped by Sandry, Frostpine (the betrayal of his parents was huge), Lark, and the reason Polyam lost her status (damn these Traders are superstitious people!).<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Fires are ravaging Gold Ridge Valley, and Duke Vedris has brought the kids to see what they can do to help.<br /><br />It's a new aspect of her magic, making metal grow, creating a net of metal that can smother fire. A skill that will save many lives and create enough <em>zokin</em> that Daja's name will be added back onto the records of the <em>Tsaw'ha</em>.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><em>Winding Circle temple</em><br /><strong>Daja Kisubo</strong> was once a Trader, but after a shipwreck in which she was the only survivor, her people have cast her out. She's <em>trangshi</em>, and she does not exist to Traders anymore. Lady Sandrilene "<strong>Sandry</strong>" is a noble, the great-niece of Duke Vedris. Her magic lies in weaving and spinning. <strong>Pirisi</strong> was her Trader nurse who died protecting her. <strong>Briar Moss</strong> was a street rat before Niko found him; now he exercises his earth magic. Trisana "<strong>Tris</strong>" Chandler loves to read and has a power over nature.<br /><br />The Dedicates who are in charge at Discipline Cottage are <strong>Rosethorn</strong>, a powerful earth dedicate with an affinity for growing whose childhood was on a farm, and <strong>Lark</strong> is a thread-mage whose skill lies with weaving whose past includes juggling and dancing. They only accept mageborn.<br /><br /><strong>Little Bear</strong> is the puppy the kids rescued in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/58889.Sandry_s_Book" target="_blank" title="Opens Tamora Pierce's Sandry's Circle in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Sandry's Circle</em>
</a>, 1. <strong>Shriek</strong> is the starling Tris rescued in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/58890.Tris_s_Book" target="_blank" title="Opens Tamora Pierce's Tris's Book in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Tris's Book</em>
</a>, 2.<br /><br /><strong>Frostpine</strong> is a smith-mage, one of the greatest and Daja's teacher. Niklaren "<strong>Niko</strong>" Goldeye is a wandering mage who finds things and people who are hidden. He's also the kids' instructor.<br /><br /><strong>Duke Vedris IV </strong>rules Emelan.<br /><br /><em>Gold Ridge Valley has its…</em><br />…own gold: saffron. <strong>Lady Inoulia fa Juzon</strong> is the valley's ruler and something of a snob. <strong>Yarrun Firetamer </strong>is the mage who puts out the fires in the valley. He's an insecure braggart whose pride and ignorance ends up killing him. His father, <strong>Ulmerin Valeward</strong>, is also a mage. <strong>Khalib ul Hanoh</strong> is the village smith where Daja creates her plant.<br /><br /><em>Traders in the Tenth Caravan Idaram</em><br />Poly<strong></strong>am is the <em>wirok</em> of Tenth Caravan Idaram, and she can't speak to Daja even though she has very low status among her people (she lost a leg in a rockslide). <strong>Chandrisa</strong> is the <em>gilav</em>! They prize cooking and bargaining.<br /><br /><em>
  <strong>Wirok</strong>
</em> buys supplies for the caravan; they bring no profit and so they are of the second lowest status. <em>
  <strong>Mimanders</strong>
</em> are Trader mages while a <em>
  <strong>xurdin</strong>
</em> is a general term for mages. A <em>
  <strong>gilav</strong>
</em> is a caravan boss. A <em>
  <strong>hamot</strong>
</em> is a fool who will accept the first offer made. <em>
  <strong>Qunsuanen</strong>
</em> is a person who has undergone <em>qunsua</em>, a ceremony that supposedly protects a Trader if she must speak with a <em>trangshi</em> *major eye roll*. <em>
  <strong>Zokin</strong>
</em> is the credit listed against your name in a Trader's ledgers and encompasses both the money you accumulate and your personal status within the caravan. <em>
  <strong>Lugsha</strong>
</em> are artisans. <em>
  <strong>Kaq</strong>
</em> is a rude word that means <em>outsider</em>. <em>
  <strong>Daka</strong>
</em> are higher-status Traders. <strong>Blue Traders</strong> travel the seas. <strong>White Traders</strong> travel in snow or sand. <em>
  <strong>Tsaw'ha</strong>
</em> is the Trader name for themselves.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is golden with its yellow green sky and a darker yellow green hazy forest with great golden blades of grass rising up from the base of the cover, both framing a black cloaked figure on a white horse.<br /><br />The title is who the focus of the story is on, for it's <em>Daja's Book</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5403618033295764838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1161808343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1161808343" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/764543-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466528802p2/764543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1161808343?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/764543-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/764543-anne?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/764543-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/764543-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/764543-anne?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161808343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer794276220549861405">I'd forgotten how this whole series takes place in such a short period of time. This one is only 4 months after Sandry's Book. And then if I remember correctly, 4 years pass between Briar's Book and the Circle Opens quartet.<br/><br/>Thoughts on relationships: for all Tamora Pierce has said that Lark and Rosethorn were together, there is SCARCE evidence of it here. Lark calls Rosethorn "Rosie" and is able to share her power with her when she won't accept anyone else's. But Rosethorn is still referred to a</span>
  <span id="freeText794276220549861405" style="display:none">I'd forgotten how this whole series takes place in such a short period of time. This one is only 4 months after Sandry's Book. And then if I remember correctly, 4 years pass between Briar's Book and the Circle Opens quartet.<br /><br />Thoughts on relationships: for all Tamora Pierce has said that Lark and Rosethorn were together, there is SCARCE evidence of it here. Lark calls Rosethorn "Rosie" and is able to share her power with her when she won't accept anyone else's. But Rosethorn is still referred to as her "friend". How anyone was supposed to pick up on this, I do not know. No signs of Daja being gay yet, either, unless we were supposed to think she's stereotypically butch because she is a smith and is always described as not having a waist.<br /><br />As for racial diversity, I hadn't picked up as a kid that both Lark and Briar were described as having some eastern/far eastern traits, or that at least one of them is mixed. I'm interested to see what else I missed as I continue with this universe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="794276220549861405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2516852636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2516852636" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21514123-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546550865p2/21514123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer18008219375555124610">This was so goooooddddd <33<br/><br/>This book picks up with Daja, Briar, Tris and Sandry in a northern area of Emelan, a place that is currently suffering from a three-year drought and some potentially nasty grass fires (which may turn into a forest fire...) and essentially get to learn more about themselves and their magic, while assisting with the area under threat. <br/><br/>The focus on Daja was clear in this one (the book title made sense, yay!) as we got to learn a lot of Daja's history as a trader, and also</span>
  <span id="freeText18008219375555124610" style="display:none">This was so goooooddddd &lt;33<br /><br />This book picks up with Daja, Briar, Tris and Sandry in a northern area of Emelan, a place that is currently suffering from a three-year drought and some potentially nasty grass fires (which may turn into a forest fire...) and essentially get to learn more about themselves and their magic, while assisting with the area under threat. <br /><br />The focus on Daja was clear in this one (the book title made sense, yay!) as we got to learn a lot of Daja's history as a trader, and also a lot about the trader culture in general - what with a large portion of this book focusing on the "trading" of an accidental creation of Daja's to a caravan of traders that were in the area.<br /><br />It made me SO MANY to see just how Daja was treated as a trangshi, and I hated how Polyam was treated by her own family purely because she'd been in an accident that caused her to lose a leg (and also her "looks" too I guess)... and that she was essentially treated as useless (which, rude). It was great that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[through Polyam (as a cripple) and Daja's (as a trangshi) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> dealings to decide how best to trade the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[magical growing metal plant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> that Daja was able to finally reconnect - at least somewhat - with her people, and that by the end Daja was welcomed back as one of them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[even if it did take her nearly killing herself (and her friends/teachers by extension) to put out a forest fire to save their lives <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The creation of that bionic limb was AWESOME and I really love how Tamora Pierce was able to combine the modern technology of today with the magic of this book to create something that was workable and believable in the environment while still making sense to the reader.<br /><br />Side note: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yarrun was a moron of the highest degree and I did not like him and his "there's only one right way to do magic and it's my way" attitude. The one-sided "dick-measuring" contest he seemed to have with Niko was also really not appreciated and need to prove his superiority as a mage was ridiculous... believable and 100% something that could happen, but he was a ridiculous man who died a ridiculous death as a result of his pride. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16954749350599595344">Sometimes the selection of audiobooks through my library (i.e., free audiobooks) are quite limited. <br/><br/>Case in point. <br/><br/>That said, this is the third --- yes, third book I've read in this series. Why? The reviews sounded great, and I think I like Tamora Pierce. I can't remember why I think that, but I do. <br/><br/>It's quite possible that this is another one of those unfortunate books (as is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_' title='The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> series) that lost its stars due to the narrator. I don't think it was a bad book, but when you're listeni</span>
  <span id="freeText16954749350599595344" style="display:none">Sometimes the selection of audiobooks through my library (i.e., free audiobooks) are quite limited. <br /><br />Case in point. <br /><br />That said, this is the third --- yes, third book I've read in this series. Why? The reviews sounded great, and I think I like Tamora Pierce. I didn't mind any of the voices except for the main narrator. She sounded like Frasier's ice queen ex-wife, Lilith. Very robotic. But get this: I looked it up, and the voice that annoyed me is the author! How funny is that?? And! One of the male voices is Bruce Coville -- and I'm in the middle of reading his Unicorn Chronicles (recommended). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114701.Into_the_Land_of_the_Unicorns__Unicorn_Chronicles___1_" title="Into the Land of the Unicorns (Unicorn Chronicles, #1) by Bruce Coville" rel="nofollow noopener">Into the Land of the Unicorns</a> Weird coincidence. <br /><br />Anyway -- I don't know if I'll get around to the 4th and last book in this series. Sorry, Tamora. I think. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34273720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6203190128937021820">The Circle books are written for a younger audience than many of Tamora Pierce's novels, but they are still excellent. <u>Daja's Book</u>, the third in the series, is almost an environmental message of a book. It is intense, more so than either of the volumes that precede it, and will keep readers on the edge of their seats. It seems to carry a message about forest care, but can also be respected as a good young adult book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4477011349386245199">A great third book in this series. I loved leaving Winding Circle and discovering more of this world. I also loved learning more about Daja's and also Frostpine's pasts. Daja has a particularly compelling journey, because not only is she confronted with her old people, who banished her, but she is also confronted with the more dangerous side of fire, which she has worked with as part of her magic every day since coming to Winding Circle. An excellent read, again.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14925673900518990485">I finally feel like one of the books in this quartet hit what I wanted. This book also has a big disaster the four kids must fight (forest fires), but unlike in the other books, it doesn't take over the whole story. Their teachers aren't saying we don't have time to teach you because of xyz thing. The forest fires are constantly going on, but also don't affect them directly for a lot of the book.<br/><br/>Because we're not focused on that, it actually gives them time to develop their relationships and the</span>
  <span id="freeText14925673900518990485" style="display:none">I finally feel like one of the books in this quartet hit what I wanted. This book also has a big disaster the four kids must fight (forest fires), but unlike in the other books, it doesn't take over the whole story. Their teachers aren't saying we don't have time to teach you because of xyz thing. The forest fires are constantly going on, but also don't affect them directly for a lot of the book.<br /><br />Because we're not focused on that, it actually gives them time to develop their relationships and their magic a bit. It feels like for so much of this book you actually get to see Daja's feelings about her own life, instead of just feelings on forest fires or pirates. There's a lot of dealing with her being exiled by her people, Traders, and missing the old life she used to have.<br /><br />The kids are also starting to get a few parameters for their magic, which is something that I didn't realize was lacking until this book. There's still kind of a sense that they can do anything with magic, which limits believability and consequences to a degree, but they're starting to learn their limits and starting to learn control.<br /><br />So far, this is my favorite of the series. I'm glad to read one that better than okay, that I was actually excited to pick up and get through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14925673900518990485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1245126815" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1245126815" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439004129p2/4881155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1245126815?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/4881155-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=protagonists-of-color">protagonists-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=target-age-group-young-adults">target-age-group-young-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4881155-whitney?shelf=female-protagonist">female-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1245126815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2260632033635835361">Daja, Tris, Briar, Sandry, and their teachers have travelled to the Gold Ridge Mountains to see if they can help with the drought that’s been going on for three years. While there, they meet with a group of Traders. When Daja, once a Trader herself, creates something so amazing that the other Traders are willing to deal with an outcast, she has a tough choice to make. Return to the Traders, her people, or stay with the people who have become like a family to her?<br/><br/><b>Plot</b><br/><br/>Just like the previous books,</span>
  <span id="freeText2260632033635835361" style="display:none">Daja, Tris, Briar, Sandry, and their teachers have travelled to the Gold Ridge Mountains to see if they can help with the drought that’s been going on for three years. While there, they meet with a group of Traders. When Daja, once a Trader herself, creates something so amazing that the other Traders are willing to deal with an outcast, she has a tough choice to make. Return to the Traders, her people, or stay with the people who have become like a family to her?<br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br /><br />Just like the previous books, pretty simple plot going on. The children and their teachers are helping Sandry’s uncle, the duke of Emelan, in Gold Ridge, a place plagued by fires from three years of drought. I realize now that while the books have strong enough plots, they explore and develop the characters more than they focus on the plot. That being said, I thought the plot was very good. This being Daja’s book, and her magic being connected to metal and fire, there was a seamless mixture of her as a character and the story being interwoven together. I’m not sure if that’s what Pierce was going for, but if she was she nailed it more in this book than the others thus far. Honestly, I have no complaints about the plot. <br /><br /><b>Writing</b><br /><br />I really liked the writing in <i>Daja’s Book</i>, probably in part because it had that blunt style of writing Pierce is much better at. There were a lot less spots in this book than in <i>Tris’s Book</i> where Peirce tried to give a vaguer, ~magical~ description of things. <i>Daja’s Book</i> was paced more quickly than the previous books, though it did have points where it lagged just a touch, but they didn’t really slow the writing down. <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br /><br />Same characters as in the last two books, but this time Daja is more the focus. I felt like Daja was characterized very well. Throughout the book the reader sees a lot more about Trader culture than ever before and certain things, like Daja not being as vocal as the other children, beings to make sense. Daja’s gets to deal with a bit of internal conflict as well, like Tris was allowed to do. I made her character all the more enticing. <br /><br />I feel like, with the third book in this four-part series, the reader is allowed to see more of the characters than the plot. I don’t know if I’m imagining things, but, even though the book was still plot driven, we received more of a look at the characters now more than ever. <br /><br /><b>Things I Liked</b><br /><br />The two things I liked most about <i>Daja’s Book</i> deal with her: the look into Trader culture and her feelings about being a trangshi. Since Daja became a trangshi way back in book one I had hoped to hear more about Traders and their culture. In this world we’re shown three major cultures: the western culture, which one could say is Emelan culture, is European based Tris and Sandry are a part of it, Trader culture, and the culture from those in the East. People know European culture so there was nothing interesting about it. Three books in and the only thing we know about the eastern culture is that it seems to be some strange mix of Chinese and Southeast Asian cultures. But Trader culture, to my knowledge, is a made up culture of its own. And it sounds fascinating. <br /><br />As luck should have it, we get to see just how Daja feels about being <i>trangshi</i>. There’s something that’s needs to be explored about a young child being kicked out of the only life she’s known and to be labelled an outcast for something that wasn’t her fault. While I personally feel like we should have gotten more hints to how she actually felt before this book, I’m glad that some of Daja’s feelings were actually addressed. Along with these feelings was the choice she made between Winding Circle and the Traders. Of course everybody knew what choice she was going to make, but I think it was presented in a very good way that allowed the readers to see more into the quietest of the youngsters. <br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Like</b><br /><br />I can’t think of anything that I didn’t particularly like (hence my rating). <br /><br /><b>Diversity</b><br /><br />Same as the last book, for the most part. The queen of Gold Ridge valley is black, and a lot of Traders don’t seem to be white. Still no transgender or confirmed non-heterosexual characters, though it looks like there’s a bit of a hint of romantic relationship between Lark and Rosethorn (but from what I’ve heard is never actually one-hundred percent confirmed in-text). There is a disabled character. She’s missing a leg and eye, and has substantial scarring. I think she was handled well, but I’m not an amputee so I can’t say for sure. <br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br /><i>Daja’s Book</i> is my favorite so far and I think it will stay that way. I loved the exploration of magic, Trader culture, and Daja’s internal thoughts and feelings. She’s not a very vocal character so seeing things for her internally added so much more to her. I would love for there to be an entire series of nothing but Daja!<br /><br /><a href="http://booknoting.tumblr.com/post/142106456150/dajas-book-notes" rel="nofollow noopener">Here is a link to my notes.</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2260632033635835361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;

    if (submit_form) {

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Remarkably strong, magically talented, a match for friend and foe<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12932507574751129421\" style=\"display:none\">With the knowing eye and fiery voice of an accomplished storyteller, Alice Borchardt takes us back to the amazing world of a re-envisioned Camelot in the continuing Tales of Guinevere. Remarkably strong, magically talented, a match for friend and foe alike, Guinevere has come into womanhood—and faces a new relationship with Lancelot that will lead to the sharp-edged triangle of legend. . . .Born of the Highlands, along Pictish shores washed by the icy North Sea, Guinevere, Queen of the Dragon People, has become a woman. She has taken the power offered to her by the Dragon Throne. Now there is no turning back. In order to protect her beloved homeland from the obscene greed of the Saxon raiders, Guinevere knows she must launch an attack. The sub-chiefs refuse to fall in line with her plans (because what does this young thing, barely a woman, know of warfare?) and give her an army of the useless, the outcast, the weakest of their young boys and girls. But the war party must proceed. If it fails, the command of both land and sea will fall to the enemy. Facing her first battle against the pirates on foreign shores, and backed only by a meager band of ill-equipped fighters, Guinevere calls upon the spirits of the dead to aid her in the attack. Diving into the dark, morbid depths, Guinevere suddenly understands more of hate, love, anger, and revenge than she has ever wanted to. But the power the dead provide comes at a severe price. If she makes it through the raid, she will be a changed woman, in more ways than she can possibly imagine. Further south, Black Leg, her childhood companion, sets out on his own. It is a quest to become a man—a man, he hopes, who will be worthy of the newly crowned Guinevere. A shapeshifter and the son of Guinevere’s adoptive man-wolf father, Black Leg (soon to be Lancelot) feels he has much to learn—and even more to prove. He discovers both his inner strength and an unmitigated passion when he meets the Lady of the Lake. But the trials of his journey— both mental and physical—turn out to be more perilous with each step. And when Lancelot and Guinevere are finally reunited, the consequences of both their ordeals will unleash a torrent of anguish and desire.With familiar names brilliantly repositioned for a new generation of Arthurian fans—evil Merlin, conniving Igrane, complex Lancelot, tainted Arthur, and of course, warrior Guinevere—Alice Borchardt’s creation stands as a testament to the power of       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">About Tamora Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9772082036449751271">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText9772082036449751271" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9772082036449751271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

"I thought you were having trouble last night. Drink this." She poured some into a cup and held it out to him.<br /><br />Niko looked at it as if she offered him rotten fish. "I am fine. I am per-" He couldn't even finish the sentence for coughing.<br /><br />"It's not bad," said Tris, crossing her fingers behind her back. "Really, tastes like-like mangoes."<br /><br />Niko looked at her, then took the cup and downed its contents. The four watched with interest as his cheeks turned pale, then scarlet. "That's terrible (exclamation point)" he cried, his voice a thin squeak.<br /><br />"Maybe I was thinking of some other syrup," Tris remarked with a straight face.&rdquo;</span>
